Faith and Disbelief
intermediate

Faith Does Not Require Justice: Quranic Evidence
Maturidi presents Quranic and consensus-based proof that faith remains despite loss of justice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Quranic verses and community consensus to argue that faith (īmān) remains even when a believer commits major sins and loses justice (ʿadāla).

Core Idea
Faith is not lost through sin; justice is a separate quality.

Maturidi now turns to the Quran and the practice of the Muslim community to refute the Muʿtazilite claim that major sins remove a person from faith. He presents a series of verses that require justice in witnesses, but the very condition of justice shows that believers can be unjust. The community's consensus on examining witnesses further proves that faith does not depend on moral perfection. Let's examine his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow of the argument. Then read the translation to understand the meaning.
Notice how Maturidi cites multiple verses in succession.
2
Identify the key verses and their implications
List the verses Maturidi quotes: 5:106, 2:282, 65:2, 4:6. For each, ask: Why does the condition prove that not all believers are just?
The condition of justice would be redundant if all believers were just.
3
Understand the logical inference and consensus
Maturidi concludes that if faith required justice, there would be no need to examine witnesses. The community's practice shows otherwise. Reflect on how this consensus refutes the Muʿtazilites.
The keyword here is 'إجماع' (consensus).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل على أن اسم الإيمان لا يزول بزوال العدالة قوله تعالى: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا شَهَادَةُ بَيْنَكُمْ إِذَا حَضَرَ أَحَدَكُمُ المَوْتَ حِينَ الوَصِيَّةِ اثْنَانِ ذَوَا عَدْلٍ مِنْكُم، ولو كان كل مؤمن عدلا لكان يقول: اثنان منكم؛ إذ كان ابتداء الآية في مخاطبة المؤمنين ثبت أن قد يكون مؤمنا عدلا وغير عدل. وقال الله تعالى: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذَا تَدَايَنْتُمْ بِدَيْنٍ إلى قوله: مِمَّنْ تَرْضَوْنَ مِنَ الشُّهَدَاءِ، فلو كان كل مؤمن مرضيا لم يكن للشرط فائدة. وكذلك قوله: وَأَشْهِدُوا ذَوِي عَدْلٍ مِنْكُمْ ثبت أن المؤمن يكون عدلا وغير عدل، وكذلك قوله: فَإِنْ آنَسْتُمْ مِنْهُمْ رُشْدًا فَادْفَعُوا إِلَيْهِمْ أَمْوَالَهُمْ، ثبت أنه قد يكون منهم رشيد وغير رشيد. ولو كان كل مؤمن عدلا وكل من ليس بعدل ليس بمؤمن لكان لا شهادة ترد بالفسق بعد الامتحان ولا يجوز السؤال عن الأحوال ليعلم بها العدالة والفسق، بل على المكان الذي يسأل عما عليه من الإيمان في ذلك ويمكنه الوفاء، فيجب قبول شهادته بلا سؤال عنه ولا اعتبار بأحواله: وفى إجماع الأمة على الفحص عن الأحوال وترك النزول على ما يظهر من الأموال التي يكتفى بها فيما كان شرائطها الإيمان من الحل والحرمة والتوارث، ثم العبادات دليل يبين أن الإيمان وما به يصير المرء مؤمنا ويستوجب أحكامه ليس هو كل ما يبقى أنواع الفسوق والعصيان، ولا قوة إلا بالله وعلى ذلك معنى أمر هذه الأمة في تعاهد الصلوات في الجماعات والصيام وإخراج الزكوات على ما عليه هم من الاختلاف في هتك الحرمات والانهماك في المعاصي، ثبت بالذي عليه الأمة عدول المعتزلة والخوارج عن الحق، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And the proof that the name of faith does not disappear with the disappearance of justice is the saying of the Most High: 'O you who have believed, testimony between you when death approaches one of you at the time of bequest is two men of justice from among you.' If every believer were just, He would say 'two from among you'; since the beginning of the verse addresses the believers, it is established that a person may be a believer just and a believer not just. And Allah Most High said: 'O you who have believed, when you contract a debt for a specified term' until His saying: 'from those you approve of among the witnesses.' If every believer were approved, the condition would have no benefit. And likewise His saying: 'And bring to witness two witnesses of justice from among you' establishes that the believer can be just and not just. And likewise His saying: 'Then if you perceive in them sound judgment, release their property to them' establishes that among them there may be one with sound judgment and one without sound judgment. And if every believer were just, and whoever is not just is not a believer, then no testimony would be rejected due to immorality after examination, and it would not be permissible to inquire about conditions to know justice and immorality; rather, immediately one would ask about his state of faith and his ability to fulfill, and his testimony would be accepted without inquiry about him and without consideration of his conditions. And the consensus of the Community (umma) on examining conditions and not relying on what appears of wealth, which suffices in matters whose conditions are faith regarding lawful, unlawful, and inheritance, then acts of worship are proof that faith and that by which a person becomes a believer and merits its rulings is not everything that remains of types of transgression and disobedience. And there is no power except with Allah. And accordingly is the meaning of the command to this Community regarding maintaining prayers in congregations, fasting, and giving zakah despite the difference among them in violating sanctities and indulging in sins. It is established by what the Community is upon that the Mu‘tazilites and the Kharijites have deviated from the truth. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 953

Commentary
This passage presents a cumulative proof from multiple Quranic verses and from the consensus of the Muslim community to establish that the name of faith (īmān) does not disappear when a person loses justice (ʿadāla) through committing major sins. Maturidi begins with verse 5:106 regarding bequests, which requires two just witnesses from among the believers. If every believer were automatically just, the specification 'of justice' would be redundant; the phrase 'from among you' would suffice. Since the condition is stated, it implies that there are believers who are just and believers who are not just. Similarly, verse 2:282 requires witnesses 'whom you approve of' among the believers, again indicating that not every believer is approved (i.e., just). Verse 65:2 similarly calls for 'two witnesses of justice from among you,' reinforcing the same point. Verse 4:6 about orphans distinguishes between those who have sound judgment (rushd) and those who do not, yet both are believers. Then Maturidi draws a logical conclusion: if faith required justice, then no testimony would ever be rejected for immorality after verification, and there would be no need to inquire into a witness's character; one would only need to ask about his faith. But the practice of the community (ijmāʿ) is to examine witnesses' moral character and to not accept testimony based solely on apparent wealth or status, which contradicts the Mu‘tazilite position. Furthermore, the observed practice of the community—obligations of prayer, fasting, and zakah—are commanded to believers, and yet they are often negligent and sinful, showing that faith remains despite sins. This consensus and practice demonstrate that the Mu‘tazilites and Kharijites have deviated from the truth by claiming that major sins remove faith.

Key Terms
الإيمان
العدالة
الشهادة
الفسق
الإجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The condition of justice in witness testimony proves that faith requires justice.
Correction: The condition actually shows that believers can be unjust; otherwise there would be no need to specify justice.

Checkpoint
What does the condition 'ذَوَا عَدْلٍ مِنْكُم' in verse 5:106 indicate according to Maturidi?
A) All believers are just
B) Believers can be either just or unjust
C) Only just people can be believers
D) Justice is the same as faith

Key Takeaway
The Quranic conditions on witnesses and the community's consensus demonstrate that a believer can be unjust and still remain a believer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim committing a major sin, do you ever doubt their faith? What would Maturidi's argument say about that, and what does your reaction reveal about your own understanding of faith?
?
Think of a time you fell into sin and felt that your faith was gone or that Allah had abandoned you. How does this passage challenge that feeling? If faith remains despite sin, what does that mean for your relationship with Allah—and what responsibility does it place on you to keep striving?
?
If justice is not a condition of faith, then what is the real condition? Look at your own heart: Is your faith anchored in your own performance or in Allah's mercy and the reality of iman as taught here? What would need to change for you to truly internalize this?

Sin Does Not Negate Faith: Qur'anic and Consensus Proofs
Maturidi uses verses and consensus to argue believers can be unjust but still faithful.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses Qur'anic verses and consensus to prove that committing sins does not negate a person's faith.

Core Idea
Faith remains intact even when a believer sins; the Qur'an and consensus confirm this.

Imam Maturidi argues against the Mu'tazilite and Kharijite claim that major sins remove a person from faith. He points to the Qur'an's own conditions—like requiring just witnesses—which would be meaningless if every believer were automatically just. He then invokes the consensus of the community in investigating moral character despite professed faith, and the fact that acts of worship are commanded even though believers commit sins. This passage establishes that faith and sin can coexist.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to get the overall argument.
Notice the logical flow: condition → deduction → consensus → worship → conclusion.
2
Identify the two Qur'anic proofs
Find the verses about witnesses (2:282) and orphans (4:6). Understand how each implies that believers can be unjust or unsound.
The condition of justice in witnesses would be useless if all believers were just.
3
Consider the hypothetical deduction
Maturidi imagines a scenario where every believer is just. He then shows it leads to absurd consequences like no need to examine witnesses.
4
Recognize the consensus argument
The community investigates people's moral character before accepting testimony or inheritance. This proves that faith does not automatically make one just.
5
Reflect on the implication against Mu'tazila and Khawarij
Maturidi concludes that the Mu'tazila and Khawarij deviated by denying faith to sinners, since the Qur'an and practice show sin does not negate faith.
This is the key sectarian point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو كان كل مؤمن مرضيا لم يكن للشرط فائدة . وكذلك قوله : " وأَشْهدُوا ذَوِي عَدْلٍ مِنْكُمْ " ثبت أن المؤمن يكون عدلا وغير عدل، وكذلك قوله : " فَإِنَّ آنَسْتُمْ مِنْهُمْ رُشْدًا فَادْفَعُوا إِلَيْهِمْ أَمْوَالَهُمْ "، ثبت أنه قديكون منهم رشيد وغير رشيد . ولو كان كل مؤمن عدلا ، وكل من ليس بعدل ليس بمؤمن لكان لا شهادة ترد بالفسق بعد الامتحان ولا يجوز السؤال عن الأحوال ليعلم بها العدالة والفسق ، بل على المكان الذي يسأل عما عليه من الإيمان في ذلك ويمكنه الوفاء ، فيجب قبول شهادته بلا سؤال عنه ولا اعتبار بأحواله : وفى إجماع الأمة على الفحص عن الأحوال وترك النزول على ما يظهر من الأموال التي يكتفى بها فيما كان شرائطها الإيمان من الحل والحرمة والتوارث ، ثم العبادات دليل يبين أن الإيمان وما به يصير المرء مؤمنا ويستوجب أحكامه ليس هو كل ما يبقى أنواع الفسوق والعصيان ، ولا قوة إلا بالله وعلى ذلك معنى أمر هذه الأمة في تعاهد الصلوات في الجماعات والصيام وإخراج الزكوات على ما عليه هم من الاختلاف في هتك الحرمات والانهماك في المعاصى ، ثبت بالذى عليه الأمة عدول المعتزلة والخوارج عن الحق ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
If every believer were acceptable, then the condition would have no benefit. Likewise His saying: 'And bring two witnesses of justice from among you' confirms that the believer may be just or not just. Likewise His saying: 'Then if you perceive in them sound judgment, deliver to them their property' confirms that among them may be sound and not sound. And if every believer were just, and whoever is not just is not a believer, then no testimony would be rejected due to immorality after examination, nor would it be permissible to ask about conditions to know justice and immorality. Rather, one should ask about what he has of faith in that [matter] and whether he can fulfill it, so his testimony must be accepted without asking about him or considering his condition. And the consensus of the community on investigating conditions and not relying on what appears of wealth—which is sufficient for matters whose conditions are faith regarding permissibility, prohibition, and inheritance—and then acts of worship are evidence that faith and that by which a person becomes a believer and earns its rulings is not all that remains of types of immorality and disobedience. There is no power but with Allah. And upon that is the meaning of the command to this community regarding maintaining prayers in congregations, fasting, and giving zakāt despite their differences in violating sanctities and being immersed in sins. It is established by what the community is upon that the Mu'tazila and Khawārij have deviated from the truth. There is no power but with Allah.
Source pages p. 954

Commentary
This passage is a proof using Qur'anic verses and consensus to show that faith does not preclude sin. The author begins with the verse on witnesses (Surah al-Baqara 2:282) and argues that if every believer were just, the condition of justice in witnesses would be pointless. He then cites the verse on orphans (Surah an-Nisa 4:6) showing that believers can be of sound judgment or not. He draws the conclusion: if faith automatically meant justice, then no testimony would need scrutiny and no inquiry into the witness's condition would be required. But the community's consensus is to investigate moral character. Moreover, acts of worship like prayer, fasting, and zakāt are commanded despite people's sins, proving that sin does not negate faith. Therefore, the Mu'tazila and Khawārij are wrong to exclude sinners from the name of faith.

Key Terms
إيمان
عدل
شهادة
إجماع
فسق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Committing a major sin entirely removes a person from faith.
Correction: Maturidi shows through Qur'anic conditions and consensus that believers can sin and still be believers.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi argue that the Qur'anic condition of justice in witnesses (Surah al-Baqara 2:282) proves that not all believers are just?
A) Because the condition would be pointless if every believer were just.
B) Because the verse explicitly says some believers are unjust.
C) Because the verse is about witnesses, not about faith.
D) Because the condition applies only to hypocrites.

Key Takeaway
Sin does not negate faith; believers can be unjust and sinful yet remain within the fold of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which sin in your life are you secretly using as evidence that you are not truly a believer? How does Maturidi's argument threaten that justification and call you to repentance instead of despair?
?
If faith coexists with sin, what is your excuse for not striving against sin? Are you using this teaching as a license to sin, or as a motivation to seek forgiveness and improve?
?
You believe you are a believer, but do you treat others as if their sins diminish their faith? How will you change your attitude toward a fellow Muslim who struggles with a public sin after understanding this lesson?

Maturidi's Refutation of al-Ka'bi on Repentance
Maturidi refutes al-Ka'bi's argument from repentance verse with three responses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi refutes al-Ka'bi's claim that the command to repent proves believers commit sin, and the three arguments he uses.

Core Idea
Repentance does not prove ongoing sin; it can be for minor sins or as worship.

Al-Ka'bi argued that the Quranic command to repent proves that believers sin, since repentance is only from sin. Imam Maturidi responds by analyzing the nature of repentance and offering three compelling refutations. This lesson examines his debate and its implications for faith and sin.

Guided Path
1
Context: al-Ka'bi's challenge
Understand al-Ka'bi's argument that the verse commanding repentance (Quran 66:8) implies that believers must have sins, because repentance is only from sin.
This sets the stage for Maturidi's response.
2
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Maturidi first presents al-Ka'bi's two possible interpretations, then gives his three responses.
Pay attention to the structure: the opponent's two ways, then three refutations.
3
Analyze Maturidi's three responses
Work through each of Maturidi's responses one by one. Understand why he rejects al-Ka'bi's interpretation and how each response undermines the argument.
The first response focuses on the meaning of repentance; the second on ingratitude; the third on the conditional nature of forgiveness.
4
Reflect on the key insight
Consider why Maturidi's refutation is significant for the relationship between faith and sin. Repentance can be commanded even for minor sins or as an act of devotion, without implying that the believer is in a state of sin.
This strengthens the position that a believer can remain faithful despite sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقال لمن احتج عليه بقوله : يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا تُوبُوا إِلَى اللَّهِ تَوْبَةً ، والتوبة لا تكون إلا عن ذنب يوجهين: أحدهما أن التوبة عن الصغيرة وإن كانت مغفورة ، والثاني على التعبد كتكرار التهليل وكدعاء الملائكة بقوله : فَاغفر لِلَّذِينَ تَابُوا ۲ نقول له : الوجه الأول دل على جهله بمعنى التوبة ، إذ هى الرجوع والندم ، ومحال ذلك عما ليس عليه ، وهو مغفور له لا يجوز عليه التعذيب ، والثاني إن حق الله عليه إذا غفر له الحمد له والشكر على العفو ، وفى التوبة كفران ذلك ، يوهم بقاءه بالتوبة ، والثالث أنه قال : عَسَى رَبُّكُم أَنْ يُكَفِّرَ عَنْكُم سَيِّئَاتِكُم ۳ ، فجعله موقوفا على ما يكفره بالتوبة ، ثبت أن الذنب باق وهو لم يزل مستحقا اسم الإيمان ، والله أعلم .
He said, responding to one who argued against him with His saying: 'O you who believe, repent to Allah with a true repentance' and that repentance is only from sin, in two ways: one, that repentance is for a minor sin even if it is forgiven; two, as an act of worship like repeating the tahlīl and like the angels' supplication in His saying: 'so forgive those who repent'. We say to him: The first way indicates ignorance of the meaning of repentance, for it is return and regret, and that is impossible concerning what one is not upon, and he is forgiven and cannot be punished. The second way: indeed Allah's right over him, when He forgives him, is praise and gratitude for pardon, while in repentance there is ingratitude for that, for it implies that he remains in need of repentance. The third way: He said: 'Perhaps your Lord will remove from you your sins', making it conditional upon what He removes through repentance. This proves that the sin remains and he has not ceased to deserve the name of faith. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 955

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. Al-Ka'bi used the verse commanding repentance (Surah at-Tahrim 66:8) to argue that believers must have sin, because repentance is only from sin. Maturidi first notes that the opponent gives two possible interpretations: (1) repentance is for a minor sin even if forgiven, or (2) it is a purely devotional act like repeating the tahlīl. Then Maturidi gives three responses: First, the interpretation that it is for a minor sin shows ignorance, because repentance is regret and returning, which cannot be for a state one is not in (i.e., the sin is forgiven). Second, if it is devotional, then commanding repentance for a forgiven sin implies ingratitude for the forgiveness, suggesting the sin is not yet forgiven. Third, the verse itself makes the removal of sins conditional on repentance ('perhaps'), proving that the sin still exists. Thus, the believer remains worthy of the name of faith despite sin.

Key Terms
توبة
ذنب
مغفور
التعبد
تهليل
كفران

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any command to repent implies the person has sinned and is currently sinful.
Correction: Repentance can be commanded for minor sins already forgiven or as an act of worship, not necessarily implying ongoing sin. Maturidi shows that the repentance verse does not prove continuous sin.

Checkpoint
What is one of Maturidi's objections to al-Ka'bi's use of the verse on repentance?
A) The verse is abrogated.
B) Repentance as regret is impossible for a forgiven sin.
C) The verse only applies to polytheists.
D) Al-Ka'bi misread the Arabic grammar.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates that the repentance verse does not prove ongoing sin; rather, repentance can be for forgiven minor sins or as worship, and the verse itself conditions forgiveness on repentance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the command 'Repent to Allah,' do you immediately assume you have committed a major sin? How does this lesson challenge that assumption? Will you now examine your heart for hidden sins you may have ignored, or consider repentance as an act of worship even when you are not aware of sin?
?
The passage defines repentance as 'return and regret.' Is your repentance marked by genuine sorrow and a turning back to Allah, or is it a mere routine? What specific step will you take today to make your next repentance more sincere?
?
Maturidi warns that commanding repentance for a forgiven sin could imply ingratitude. Do you ever feel compelled to 'repent again' for past sins that Allah has already forgiven? How does this lesson free you from that burden? Write a commitment to trust in Allah's forgiveness and stop doubting His pardon.

Why Commanding Repentance for a Forgiven Sin is Invalid
Maturidi explains why commanding tawba for a forgiven sin is invalid and akin to inappropriate du'a.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why it is invalid to command repentance for a sin that has already been forgiven, and how this relates to ingratitude for blessings and the nature of worship.

Core Idea
Commanding repentance for a forgiven sin implies ingratitude, because it denies the forgiveness already granted.

Maturidi continues his refutation by examining the logical consequences of commanding repentance for a forgiven sin. He argues that such a command would imply the sin remains unforgiven, which is a form of ingratitude for Allah's blessings. He contrasts this with commands to recite tahlīl, which are permissible without any sin, and draws an analogy with inappropriate supplication. Let us explore this argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basis: repentance is only for sin
Read the first part of the passage where Maturidi states that the reality of actions is that they do not remain, and repentance is for a sin. If there is no sin (because it is forgiven), then commanding repentance is meaningless.
This sets the foundation: repentance is tied to sin, not a general act of worship.
2
Contrast with permissible worship: tahlīl
Notice that Maturidi says commanding tahlīl is permissible as an act of worship even without sin, but commanding tawba and istighfar for a forgiven sin is not because it suggests the sin is not forgiven.
Tahlīl is a pure act of devotion, while tawba inherently implies prior sin.
3
Reflect on the analogy with supplication
Consider the example of supplicating to Allah not to wrong or oppress – this is inappropriate because it implies the possibility of wrongdoing. Similarly, angels' supplication for forgiveness is only for those with unforgiven sins. This reinforces the argument.
The analogy shows that certain forms of speech can imply something false about Allah's attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأنه والتسهيل له في كل وقت حكم التحديد؛ لأن حقيقة الأفعال أن لا يبقى والتوبة يكون عن ذنب، ولا ذنب. وبعد، فإنه يجوز الأمر بالتهليل على التعبد ولا يجوز بالتوبة والاستغفار عن ذنب مغفور؛ لما فيه إيهام أنه ليس بمغفور، وذلك كفران النعم، وغير جائز ذلك، كما لا يجوز الدعاء بأن لا يجوز ولا يظلم، ودعاء الملائكة؛ لما قد يكون لمن ذكر ذنوبا غير مغفورة، فإلى ذلك ينصرف الدعاء، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
Because ease for him at every time is the ruling of specification; for the reality of actions is that they do not remain, and repentance is for a sin, and there is no sin. Moreover, it is permissible to command tahlīl as an act of worship, and it is not permissible to command repentance and seeking forgiveness for a forgiven sin, because it implies that it is not forgiven, and that is ingratitude for blessings, and that is not permissible, just as supplication is not permissible for that He should not wrong and not oppress, and the supplication of the angels—because it may be for one who has mentioned sins that are not forgiven, so the supplication is directed to that. There is no power but with Allah.
Source pages p. 955

Commentary
This passage continues the refutation of the previous argument. Maturidi states that the 'ease' given to the sinner (the command to repent) is actually a specification of the ruling; it does not mean the sin remains. The reality of actions is that they do not persist. Repentance is only for a sin, but if there is no sin (because it is forgiven), commanding repentance is invalid. Then he contrasts commanding tahlīl (saying 'there is no god but Allah') as a devotional act, which is permissible even without prior sin. But commanding tawba and istighfar for a forgiven sin is not permissible because it implies that the sin is not yet forgiven, which is ingratitude for Allah's forgiveness. Similarly, it is not permissible to supplicate to Allah asking Him not to wrong or oppress, because that would imply He could do so. The angels' supplication for forgiveness is directed only to those who have unforgiven sins, not to those already forgiven. Thus, the verse commanding repentance cannot be used to say believers commit sins.

Key Terms
توبة
استغفار
تهليل
كفران النعم
دعاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Commanding repentance for a forgiven sin is acceptable because it is a form of worship.
Correction: Maturidi argues that such a command implies that the sin is not yet forgiven, which is ingratitude for the blessing of forgiveness. Worship like tahlīl does not imply sin and is permissible.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi consider commanding repentance for a forgiven sin to be 'ingratitude for blessings' (kufrān al-ni'am)?
A) Because it suggests that Allah's forgiveness is insufficient.
B) Because it implies the sin is not yet forgiven.
C) Because it rejects the obligation to thank Allah.
D) Because it is a form of polytheism.

Key Takeaway
Commanding repentance for a sin that Allah has already forgiven is invalid because it implies ingratitude for the forgiveness, just as asking Allah not to wrong implies the possibility of wrongdoing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about a past sin that you have sincerely repented from, do you still feel the need to constantly seek forgiveness for it? How does holding onto that guilt or re-repenting reflect ingratitude for Allah's complete forgiveness?
?
In your du'a, do you ever ask Allah not to wrong you or to be fair to you? What does that reveal about your belief in Allah's justice and mercy, and how can you rephrase your supplications to avoid implying ingratitude or lack of trust?
?
The lesson says that commanding tawba for a forgiven sin is like kufr al-ni'm. Are you truly living as one who has been fully pardoned, or do you habitually return to old 'used-to-be-sins' in your mind as if they still define you? What would it mean for you today to accept that His forgiveness is final?

Understanding Maturidi's Interpretation of 'Why Do You Say What You Do Not Do'
Maturidi interprets the verse as a prohibition against future sin, not a report of past sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's interpretation of Qur'an 61:2 as a prohibition against future sin, not a report of past hypocrisy.

Core Idea
The verse is a warning, not a rebuke.

Maturidi carefully refutes a potential misinterpretation of Qur'an 61:2. Some might think this verse condemns believers for not acting on their faith. But Maturidi shows, through a clear example, that the verse is a preventive warning against future sin, not a statement about past failure.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the structure: Maturidi begins by quoting the verse, then explains its meaning with an example.
The Arabic uses a conditional structure 'except that this is about something that one has not done.'
2
Identify the key interpretive move
Observe how Maturidi shifts the understanding from a reported past action to a future hypothetical. He argues that the verse addresses something not yet done.
This is a key principle in Maturidi's methodology: defending believers from accusations of hypocrisy.
3
Understand the example given
Maturidi gives an analogy: a person sees another being tempted by misleaders to do something evil, and says 'Why would you do that?' as a warning, not as an accusation.
The phrase 'ما ينقص دينك' highlights the harmful consequence; the warning is out of care.
4
Connect to broader Maturidi methodology
This interpretation shows Maturidi's effort to uphold the integrity of believers by showing that Qur'anic reproaches are often preventive, not condemnations of past acts.
This is a pattern in his commentary: protecting the faith of Muslims against over-literalism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال فى قوله : يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لِمَ تَقُولُونَ مَا لَا تَفْعَلُونَ ، إلا أن ذا يكون فيما لم يكن فعله كمن يرى آخر يدعوه بعض الغواة إلى أمر قبيح فيقول على سبيل النهى : لم تفعل يا أخى ما ينقص دينك ويوجب عليك سخط ربك، لا أنه فعله، لكن لئلا يفعله.
Then he said concerning His saying: 'O you who believe, why do you say what you do not do' except that this is about something that one has not done, like one who sees another being called by some misleaders to a despicable matter and says by way of prohibition: 'Why would you do, O my brother, what diminishes your religion and necessitates your Lord's displeasure?' not that he has done it, but [he says it] so that he will not do it.
Source pages p. 955

Commentary
This passage is an interpretation of the Qur'anic verse (Surah as-Saff 61:2). Maturidi refutes al-Ka'bi's possible use of this verse to argue that believers say they believe but do not act. He explains that the verse is about a future hypothetical action, not a statement of something already done. The example given is of a person who sees another being tempted by deviant people to do something evil. The person says, 'Why would you do that which diminishes your religion and incurs your Lord's anger?' This is a preventive warning, not an accusation that the person has already committed the act. Thus, the verse does not imply that believers have committed sins contrary to their faith.

Key Terms
لم تقولون ما لا تفعلون
نهى
غواة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the verse rebukes believers for past hypocrisy—claiming faith but not acting on it.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the verse is a preventive warning against future sin, not a report of past failure.

Checkpoint
How does Maturidi interpret the verse 'Why do you say what you do not do' (Surah as-Saff 61:2)?
A) As a rebuke for past hypocrisy.
B) As a prohibition against future sin, like a warning.
C) As a command to always do what you say.
D) As a statement that all believers are hypocrites.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi shows that the verse is a preventive warning, protecting believers from future sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a command from Allah, do you immediately think about how you have failed in the past, or do you genuinely consider it as a warning to protect your future? Which perspective does Maturidi's interpretation encourage, and how does that change your response to divine commands?
?
Think of a time someone warned you against a sin. Did you take it as an accusation or as protective counsel? How does Maturidi's analogy reframe your understanding of such warnings, and will you receive them differently now?
?
The verse directly addresses believers: 'O you who believe, why do you say what you do not do?' If Allah confronted you with this question today about any area of your life, what would be your honest answer? What specific gap between your profession of faith and your actions will you work to close starting this week?

Maturidi's Refutation of Repentance Implying Prior Sin
Maturidi refutes an objection about the verse commanding repentance from sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the command to repent does not imply that believers remain in unforgiven sin, and why repentance only applies to actual sins.

Core Idea
Repentance means regret for a sin, not for something already forgiven.

An opponent argued that the Quranic command to repent (Surah al-Tahrim 66:8) proves that believers must repent from sin, thus they must have unforgiven sins. Imam Maturidi refutes this by examining the meaning of repentance and the logic of the verse. In this passage, he shows why repentance only makes sense when directed at an actual sin, not at a forgiven one, and how the verse's own structure supports this.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get an overview of Maturidi's refutation.
Notice the density of the argument; multiple points are compressed.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponent uses the verse 'O you who have believed, repent to Allah with a repentance' to argue that repentance is only from sin, thus believers must have sins.
3
Follow Maturidi's three responses
The passage presents three key refutations: the meaning of tawba, the ingratitude of repenting for a forgiven act, and the verse's own wording indicating sin remains.
Each response is based on the nature of repentance and the context of the verse.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Understand that repentance only applies to actual sins, not to what is forgiven, and that the believer remains in faith even while sin is expiated.
Consider the comparison with tahlil and angelic supplications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقال لمن احتج عليه بقوله : يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا تُوبُوا إِلَى اللَّهِ تَوْبَةً ، والتوبة لا تكون إلا عن ذنب يوجهين: أحدهما أن التوبة عن الصغيرة وإن كانت مغفورة ، والثاني على التعبد كتكرار التهليل وكدعاء الملائكة بقوله : فَاغْفر لِلَّذِينَ تَابُوا نقول له : الوجه الأول دل على جهله بمعنى التوبة ، إذ هى الرجوع والندم ، ومحال ذلك عما ليس عليه ، وهو مغفور له لا يجوز عليه التعذيب ، والثاني إن حق الله عليه إذا غفر له الحمد له والشكر على العفو ، وفى التوبة كفران ذلك ، يوهم بقاءه بالتوبة ، والثالث أنه قال : عَسَى رَبُّكُم أَنْ يُكَفِّرَ عَنْكُم سَيِّئَاتِكُم ، فجعله موقوفا على ما يكفره بالتوية ، ثبت أن الذنب باق وهو لم يزل [مستحقا] اسم الإيمان ، والله أعلم . لأنه والتسهيل له في كل وقت حكم التحديد ؛ لأن حقيقة الأفعال أن لا يبقى والتوبة يكون عن ذنب ، ولا ذنب . وبعد ، فإنه يجوز الأمر بالتهليل على التعبد ولا يجوز بالتوبة والاستغفار عن ذنب مغفور ؛ لما فيه إيهام أنه ليس بمغفور ، وذلك كفران النعم ، وغير جائز ذلك ، كما لا يجوز الدعاء بأن لا يجوز ولا يظلم ، ودعاء الملائكة ؛ لما قد يكون لمن ذكر ذنوبا غير مغفورة ، فإلى ذلك ينصرف الدعاء ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
He said addressing one who argued against him with His saying: 'O you who have believed, repent to Allah with a repentance.' Repentance is only from a sin, with two aspects: first, that repentance from a minor sin even if it is forgiven; second, as an act of devotion like repeating the tahlil and like the supplication of the angels in His saying: 'So forgive those who repent.' We say to him: The first aspect indicates his ignorance of the meaning of repentance, for it is return and regret, and that is impossible for what is not upon him, and he is forgiven and not subject to punishment. The second: indeed the right of Allah upon him when He forgives him is praise and gratitude for pardon, and in repentance there is ingratitude for that, implying its continuation by repentance. The third: he said: 'Perhaps your Lord will expiate for you your evil deeds,' making it dependent on what He expiates by repentance, proving that the sin remains and that he has not ceased being [deserving] the name of faith, and Allah knows best. Because making it easy for him at every time is the ruling of limitation; for the reality of actions is that they do not persist, and repentance is from a sin, and there is no sin. Moreover, it is permissible to command tahlil as an act of devotion, but it is not permissible to command repentance and seeking forgiveness for a sin that is forgiven; because it implies that it is not forgiven, and that is ingratitude for blessings, and that is not permissible, just as it is not permissible to supplicate that one not be made to suffer or be wronged, and the supplication of the angels, because it may be for those who have mentioned unforgiven sins, and thus the supplication is directed to that. There is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 955

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an opponent who used the verse commanding repentance (Surah al-Tahrim 66:8) to argue that repentance implies a prior sin, thus claiming that a believer who commits a major sin must repent and therefore loses the name of faith until repentance. Maturidi identifies two aspects of the objection: first, that repentance from a minor sin even if forgiven, and second, that repentance is an act of devotion like repeating the tahlil. Maturidi responds: The first aspect shows ignorance of repentance's meaning—it is return and regret, impossible for someone who is already forgiven and not subject to punishment. The second: if Allah has forgiven, one should praise and thank, but repentance would imply ingratitude. A third point: the verse 'Perhaps your Lord will expiate' shows that the sin is still present and requires expiation, so the sin remains while the believer still holds the name of faith. Maturidi further argues that commanding repentance for a forgiven sin is like implying it is not forgiven, which is ingratitude. He compares it to supplications that assume sins are unforgiven. Thus repentance is only for actual sins, not for forgiven ones.

Key Terms
توبة (tawba)
ذنب (dhanb)
مغفور (maghfūr)
تعبد (taʿabbud)
إيمان (īmān)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That repentance (tawba) is always required for forgiveness.
Correction: Maturidi shows it is only meaningful when a sin is not yet forgiven; repenting for a forgiven sin is ingratitude.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why is it invalid to argue that the verse commanding repentance proves that believers commit unforgiven sins?
A) Because repentance is only for minor sins, not major ones.
B) Because repentance (tawba) means return and regret, which is impossible for a forgiven sin.
C) Because the verse abrogates the need for repentance.
D) Because sin and faith cannot coexist.

Key Takeaway
Repentance (tawba) is regret for sin, so it only applies when sin exists; commanding it for a forgiven sin would contradict Allah's forgiveness and imply ingratitude.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you dwelled on a past sin that Allah has already forgiven? This lesson teaches that repentance is only for sins that are not yet forgiven. Are you guilty of ingratitude by treating Allah's forgiveness as incomplete? Commit today to replace unnecessary remorse with active gratitude for His pardon.
?
The opponent assumed that a believer must always be repenting from some sin to maintain faith. Have you ever felt that your faith is only valid when you are constantly aware of your failures? How does Maturidi's argument free you from that false guilt, and what will you do to embrace the reality that your faith remains even when sin lingers?
?
If commanding repentance for a forgiven sin implies that the sin is not forgiven, then what does your constant self-criticism and re-repentance for past forgiven sins say about your trust in Allah's forgiveness? Will you, from this moment, stop treating forgiven sins as if they still need repentance, and instead channel that energy into praise and thanks?

Maturidi's Interpretation of 'Why Do You Say What You Do Not Do'
Maturidi interprets verse 61:2 and refutes those who misuse it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the verse 'Why do you say what you do not do' (61:2) is a prohibition against future sin, not a confession of past sin, and its implications for the status of believers who commit major sins.

Core Idea
The verse warns against future sin, not confessing past sin.

This passage from Imam Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid addresses a common misinterpretation of Quran 61:2. Some had argued that the verse proves that believers who commit major sins are hypocrites. Maturidi firmly rejects this, offering an alternative reading: the verse is a prohibition, like warning someone not to do something wrong. The passage then turns polemical, accusing opponents of audacity against Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without analysis. Then read the English translation. Notice the structure: first the interpretation, then the refutation.
The passage is dense and polemical.
2
Understand Maturidi's interpretation
Maturidi explains that the verse is like saying 'Why do you do that?' to prevent someone from sinning. The speaker is not confessing to having done it himself.
This is the core of his argument.
3
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponent uses the verse to deny the faith of a believer who commits a major sin. Maturidi responds harshly, stating this is audacity against Allah.
Note the strong language: 'fabrication', 'Satanic insinuation'.
4
Reflect on the theological significance
This passage defends the Sunni position that a major sinner remains a believer. Maturidi warns against excommunicating fellow Muslims.
This is a key point in faith-and-disbelief debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال فى قوله : يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لِمَ تَقُولُونَ مَا لَا تَفْعَلُونَ ، إلا أن ذا يكون فيما لم يكن فعله كمن يرى آخر يدعوه بعض الغواة إلى أمر قبيح فيقول على سبيل النهى : لم تفعل يا أخى ما ينقص دينك ويوجب عليك سخط ربك ، لا أنه فعله ، لكن لئلا يفعله . فيقال له : إن كان جهدك فى صرف اسم الإيمان عن المبتلى بكبيرة – على أنت به فلك ما اخترت لثلا تسمى ما فيه من تعظيم الرحمن وخشية العواقب في نفسك وسويته ، وإن كان ذلك لتزيل هذا عن غيرك فهو يعلم جرأتك في ذلك على الله بما فهم من تسمية الله إياه بغير الذى سميته ، فلا يحتمل أن يرتاب نفسه كذلك بافترائك على الله بتسويل الشيطان ، في خبر الله ، مع ما يعلم من ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم الذي ذكرته لا يحتمله إلا سفيه أن يقول ويعاقب على ما يعلم كذبه فيما يعاتبه عليه ، فأما الله سبحانه الذى لا يخفى عليه شيء يتعالى عن هذه الرتبة التي يأنف منها كل ذي لب ، والله المستعان . وأما أنت فحقيق لذلك لأنك تيأس به من روح الله وتؤثر شهوتك عداوة الله وولاية الشيطان ويتعرك فى مذهبه لمقته ولعنه ، فهنيئا لك ما اخترته لنفسك عند الكريم والرحيم ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
Then he said regarding His saying: 'O you who have believed, why do you say what you do not do?' except that this applies to what one has not done, like someone who sees another being called by some misguided people to a reprehensible act, so he says by way of prohibition: 'Why do you do, O my brother, what diminishes your religion and incurs your Lord's anger?' not that he did it, but so that he does not do it. So it is said to him: If your effort is to remove the name of faith from one afflicted with a major sin – I leave you to it, you have what you chose [for yourself]; lest you call what is in it of glorification of the All-Merciful and fear of consequences in yourself and others? And if that is to remove this from others, then He knows your audacity in that against Allah, from what He understands of Allah's naming him with something other than what you named him. So he cannot doubt himself likewise because of your fabrication against Allah through the insinuation of Satan, in the report of Allah, along with what he knows of. There is no power except with Allah. Then what you mentioned cannot be borne except by a fool who says and is punished for what he knows is false in what he rebukes him for. As for Allah Almighty, from whom nothing is hidden, He is exalted above this level from which every intelligent person is averse. God is the Succorer. As for you, you deserve that because you despair of the mercy of Allah, prefer your lust to the enmity of Allah and the friendship of Satan, and are entangled in his doctrine for his spite and curse. So congratulations for what you have chosen for yourself before the Generous and Merciful. There is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 955

Commentary
This passage is an interpretation and defense of the verse 'Why do you say what you do not do' (Surah al-Saff 61:2). Maturidi explains that the verse is not a confession of sin but a prohibition: it applies to something one has not yet done, like someone warning another against a sinful act by saying 'Why do you do that?' without having done it himself. Then he turns to an opponent who uses this verse to argue that believers who commit major sins are not true believers. Maturidi responds harshly: if the opponent tries to remove the name of faith from a sinner, he is audacious against Allah, because Allah has called such a person a believer. The opponent's argument is based on fabrication and Satanic insinuation. He concludes that such a position is only held by a fool who deserves punishment, while Allah is beyond such lowly reasoning. The tone is polemical, defending the Sunni view that a major sinner remains a believer.

Key Terms
لِمَ تَقُولُونَ (lima taqūlūn)
إيمان (īmān)
كبيرة (kabīra)
افتراء (iftirā')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Why do you say what you do not do' proves that believers who sin are hypocrites and not true believers.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that the verse is a prohibition against doing something bad in the future, not a confession of having done it. It cannot be used to deny the faith of a believer who commits a major sin.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the correct interpretation of 'Why do you say what you do not do'?
A) It rebukes hypocrites who claim faith but do not act.
B) It is a prohibition against a future action, not a confession of having done it.
C) It applies only to the Prophet and his companions.
D) It proves that believers cannot sin.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi interprets Quran 61:2 as a prohibition against future sin, not a confession, and strongly condemns those who use it to deny the faith of fellow believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used a Quranic verse to judge another Muslim's faith because of a sin you saw in them? What does Maturidi's stern rebuke of that attitude reveal about the state of your own heart? Will you repent and ask Allah's forgiveness for such audacity?
?
Maturidi says that denying the name of faith to a sinner is a fabrication against Allah. Is there any hidden pride in you that makes you see yourself as more of a believer than others? How can you actively combat that pride today by seeing your own sinfulness and relying on Allah's mercy?
?
If you truly internalize that the verse 'Why do you say what you do not do' is a prohibition for yourself to avoid sin, not a weapon against others, how will that change the way you speak about your own failures and the way you advise fellow believers? What specific step will you take this week to warn with mercy instead of condemn?

Faith Remains Despite Lack of Humility
Maturidi argues faith remains despite lack of khushūʿ using Quranic address.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Quranic verse 57:16 to argue that the name of faith remains for believers who commit major sins like lack of humility.

Core Idea
Faith is not negated by sin; the Quran addresses believers before commanding humility.

This passage presents Maturidi's argument from the verse 'Has the time not come...' He shows that Allah addresses the believers as believers before telling them to be humble, proving that faith persists even without perfect humility. This refutes those who claim major sins remove one from faith entirely. The faqih then reinforces this by noting that the verse indicates major sin while preserving the name of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Pay attention to the structure: two points introduced by 'first' and 'second'.
The faqih's comment follows the second point.
2
Examine the two arguments
Maturidi makes two arguments from the verse: (1) the verse affirms faith before mentioning humility, (2) rhetorical reminders do not deny the attribute. Identify each in the text.
3
Understand the refutation
The faqih explains that the verse shows blameworthiness and major sin, but still calls them believers. This directly invalidates the opponent's claim that sinners lose the name of faith.
This is the key doctrinal point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال : في قوله تعالى : (أَلَمْ يَأْنِ لِلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا أَنْ تَخْشَعَ قُلُوبُهُمْ لِذِكْرِ اللَّهِ إنه أثبت اسم الإيمان وإن لم تخشع قلوبهم ، إن أول ذلك إثبات اسم الإيمان بلا خشوع ، وأنتم لا ترون إلا التصديق باللسان والمعرفة بالقلب ، / والثاني أن قد يقول لمن يخشى الله ويقوم بالغاية فى شكره : أما ينبغي لك أن تخشاني وتشكرني لا أنه غير شاكر له ، ولكن على التنبيه قال الفقيه رحمه الله : فأما الأول فإنما الآية إنما هو في الخشوع لذكر الله ، وأن من لا يخشع له مذموم فاسق ، وخشوع الإيمان هو الذي يكون بمعرفة جلاله وكبريائه ، وهذا لا يزول عن المؤمن ، ومع الإيمان قد سمى مؤمنا وإن كان به مذموما ، وفى الآية دلالة طول ذلك فيهم ، وذلك يوجب الوصف بالكبيرة عندهم ، وقد أبقى لهم اسم الإيمان فبطل بذلك قولهم ، والله الموفق .
Then he said regarding the saying of the Most High: 'Has the time not come for those who have believed that their hearts should be humble to the remembrance of Allah?' He affirmed the name of faith even if their hearts are not humble. First, that is affirmation of the name of faith without humility, while you only see faith as affirmation by the tongue and knowledge by the heart. Second, it may be said to one who fears Allah and exceeds in gratitude: 'Should you not fear Me and thank Me?' – not that he is not grateful, but as a reminder. The faqih, may Allah have mercy on him, said: As for the first, the verse is about humility to the remembrance of Allah, and one who does not have it is blameworthy and a transgressor. The humility of faith is that which comes from knowledge of His majesty and greatness, and this does not depart from the believer. With faith, he is called a believer even if he is blameworthy. The verse indicates the length of that state among them, and that necessitates the description of major sin according to them, yet it preserved for them the name of faith, so their statement is invalidated. Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 956

Commentary
This passage is an argument using the verse 'Has the time not come for those who have believed that their hearts should be humble to the remembrance of Allah?' (Surah al-Hadid 57:16). Maturidi points out that the verse addresses 'those who have believed' and then says their hearts should be humble, implying they are believers even before achieving humility. This refutes those who say that major sins (like lack of humility) remove faith. Maturidi adds a second point: such expressions can be used as reminders, not as denials of the attribute. The faqih then comments: the verse shows that lack of khushūʿ (humility) is blameworthy and a major sin, but the people are still called believers. This directly contradicts the view of those who deny the name of faith to sinners, because the verse preserves the name of faith despite the sin. Thus the opponent's argument is invalid.

Key Terms
خشوع (khushūʿ)
إيمان (īmān)
فاسق (fāsiq)
كبيرة (kabīra)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One who commits major sins, like lacking humility in prayer, is no longer a believer.
Correction: The verse shows that believers can be blameworthy (fasiq) and still be called believers, so major sins do not remove the name of faith.

Checkpoint
How does the verse 'Has the time not come for those who have believed that their hearts should be humble' refute the claim that sin removes faith?
A) It says only believers can be humble.
B) It addresses the believers before commanding humility, showing they are believers even without it.
C) It commands humility only for hypocrites.
D) It proves that sins are forgiven for believers.

Key Takeaway
The verse 'Has the time not come...' proves that believers remain believers even when lacking humility, refuting those who say major sins remove faith.

?

What does it mean for you that Allah still calls you a believer even when your heart is hard? Will you let that grace soften you today, or will you stay comfortable?
?
Maturidi says the verse affirms faith even without khushūʿ. Does this truth make you more grateful for Allah's mercy, or does it tempt you to be complacent about your negligence in prayer? What is one specific change in your prayer or remembrance you will commit to before tomorrow?
?
The verse asks a question that implies a rebuke: 'Has the time not come?' If you honestly examine your heart, what would you say? Is there an area of your life where you have delayed obeying Allah? Write down one concrete step you will take today to demonstrate that your faith is alive.

Refutation of the Mu'tazilite Use of Quran 57:16 on Faith and Sin
Imam Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazilite interpretation of Quran 57:16 regarding faith and sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazilite interpretation of Quran 57:16, demonstrating that major sin does not negate faith.

Core Idea
Major sin does not remove the name of faith; the believer remains a believer even when blameworthy.

The Mu'tazila cite Quran 57:16 to argue that faith can exist without humility, but Imam Maturidi shows that the verse actually supports the position that a sinner retains the name of faith. This lesson unpacks his argument, distinguishing between the humility that is essential to faith and the blameworthy lack of attention.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally.
Notice the structure: opponent's two points then author's detailed response.
2
Identify the opponent's two points
The Mu'tazila make two claims from the verse. First, that faith is affirmed without humility. Second, that the rebuke is for someone already grateful, as an exhortation.
3
Understand the author's distinction
Imam Maturidi distinguishes two types of khushu': the humility of faith (knowledge of Allah's majesty) which never leaves a believer, and the lack of attention to remembrance, which is blameworthy. The verse rebukes the latter while retaining the name of faith.
This shows that major sin does not remove the name of believer.
4
See the conclusion
The author concludes that the verse retains 'iman' for the sinner, invalidating the Mu'tazilite position that major sin negates faith. The second point is also refuted by showing the absurdity of applying the verse to Allah in the way they do.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : في قوله تعالى : (أَلَمْ يَأْنِ لِلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا أَنْ تَخْشَعَ قُلُوبُهُمْ لِذِكْرِ اللَّهِ ۲ إنه أثبت اسم الإيمان وإن لم تخشع قلوبهم ، إن أول ذلك إثبات اسم الإيمان بلا خشوع ، وأنتم لا ترون إلا التصديق باللسان والمعرفة بالقلب ، والثاني أن قد يقول لمن يخشى الله ويقوم بالغاية فى شكره : أما ينبغي لك أن تخشاني وتشكرني لا أنه غير شاكر له ، ولكن على التنبيه قال الفقيه رحمه الله : فأما الأول فإنما الآية إنما هو في الخشوع لذكر الله ، وأن من لا يخشع له مذموم فاسق ، وخشوع الإيمان هو الذي يكون بمعرفة جلاله وكبريائه ، وهذا لا يزول عن المؤمن ، ومع الإيمان قد سمى مؤمنا وإن كان به مذموما ، وفى الآية دلالة طول ذلك فيهم ، وذلك يوجب الوصف بالكبيرة عندهم ، وقد أبقى لهم اسم الإيمان فبطل بذلك قولهم ، والله الموفق . والثانى هو وصف من لا يعرف المنة والشكر فيعرض عن قبولهما ويعاتب على ما كان حقه التعظيم والقبول ، فإن كان هذا وصف الله عند المعتزلة فهو قد من التسمى بأقبح اسم والخلود في أسفل الدرك ، نعوذ بالله من الشقاء . ثم أطنب فى هذا القول ، لكن من أصل بنائه ما ذكت ، فما نريد إطنابه إلا بعدا عن الإصابة ، وبالله المعونة .
He said: Regarding His statement, the Exalted: 'Has not the time come for those who have believed that their hearts should be humbled for the remembrance of Allah...' (57:16) — indeed He affirmed the name of faith (iman) even if their hearts are not humbled. The first point is that He affirmed the name of faith without humility (khushu'), and you (Mu'tazila) only accept verbal confession (tasdiq bil-lisan) and knowledge of the heart (ma'rifa bil-qalb). The second point is that He may say to one who fears Allah and stands at the utmost in His gratitude: 'Should you not fear Me and thank Me?' — not that he is not grateful, but as an exhortation. The jurist (al-faqih), may Allah have mercy on him, said: As for the first point, the verse is about humility for the remembrance of Allah, and one who does not have humility is blameworthy and a sinner (fasiq). The humility of faith is that which comes from knowledge of His majesty and grandeur, and this does not depart from the believer. With faith, he is called a believer even though he is blameworthy. In the verse there is an indication of the duration of that (sin) among them, and that necessitates the description of major sin (kabira) for them, and He has retained for them the name of faith, so their statement is invalidated. And Allah is the Success. The second point: It is the description of one who does not acknowledge the favor and gratitude, so he turns away from accepting them and is rebuked for what should have been veneration and acceptance. If this is the description of Allah according to the Mu'tazila, then he (the sinner) has been described with the most ugly name and eternal punishment in the lowest depth — we seek refuge with Allah from misery. Then he went on at length in this statement, but it is from the foundation of his construction as we mentioned, so we do not desire his verbosity except as a departure from correctness. And with Allah is the help.
Source pages p. 956

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The opponent (Mu'tazila) cites Quran 57:16 to argue that faith can exist without humility (khushu'), proposing two points: first, the verse affirms faith even without humility; second, the verse rebukes someone who already fears and thanks Allah, as an exhortation, not because he is ungrateful. The author (Imam Maturidi) responds by distinguishing between two types of khushu': the khushu' of faith (which is knowledge of Allah's majesty and never leaves the believer) and lack of khushu' for remembrance, which is blameworthy. The verse retains the name 'believer' for the sinner, proving that major sin does not negate faith. The author then addresses the opponent's second point, arguing that if the description in the verse refers to Allah (as the Mu'tazila claim), then it would wrongly describe the sinner with the worst attributes and eternal punishment, which is absurd. The author concludes that the opponent's verbosity only leads away from truth.

Key Terms
إيمان
خشوع
كبيرة
فاسق
تصديق
معرفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse suggests that a believer can lack all humility and still be considered a believer in the same way as a pious believer.
Correction: The verse rebukes a lack of attention to remembrance, but the essential humility of faith (knowledge of Allah's majesty) remains. The believer is still called a believer despite being blameworthy.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Maturidi's response, what does the verse (57:16) prove about a believer who commits a major sin?
A) He is no longer a believer.
B) He retains the name of faith despite being blameworthy.
C) His faith is invalid unless he has khushu' at all times.
D) He is a disbeliever until he repents.

Key Takeaway
The verse retains the name of faith for the sinner, proving that major sin does not expel one from the fold of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite Quran or make dhikr, do you sense the 'humility of faith' (knowledge of Allah's majesty) in your heart, or do you find yourself performing the act mechanically? What one change will you make today to ensure your remembrance is accompanied by that inner khushu'?
?
The verse retains the name 'believer' for those who sin. Does this comfort you into complacency about your own sins, or does it spur you to strive for a state where you are not blameworthy? Be honest: which has been your attitude this past week?
?
The Mu'tazila believed that a major sinner is no longer a believer, which leads to despair. How does your belief about the permanence of faith (despite sin) affect the way you treat a fellow Muslim who struggles with a major sin? Will you change anything in your behavior after this lesson?

Imam Maturidi's Refutation of the Mu'tazilite Argument from Surah al-Hujurat
Imam Maturidi responds to the Mu'tazilite argument from the verse about fighting believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi refutes the claim that fighting between believers removes faith, using Quranic evidence and logical reasoning.

Core Idea
Fighting believers do not lose faith; Allah still calls them brothers despite transgression.

The Mu'tazilites argued that because Allah commands fighting against a transgressing group in Quran 49:9, that group must have lost their faith. Imam Maturidi responds by carefully analyzing the same verse, showing that Allah retains the titles 'believers' and 'brothers' for them, and that fighting does not necessarily negate iman. This lesson unpacks his two main responses and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation once. Notice the structure: the opponent's argument is implied, and the author gives two responses.
2
Identify the two responses
The passage presents two distinct answers. The first compares the verse to the apostasy verse (2:217). The second considers that the fighting might be without weapons or based on ijtihad.
Look for the words 'أول' and 'ثاني' in the Arabic.
3
Understand the further reasoning
After the two responses, the author adds that the command to reconcile and the retention of the name 'brothers' invalidates apostasy. He also argues that the command to fight the transgressor shows the transgression was known, not an ijtihad error.
4
Reflect on the main conclusion
The passage concludes that even if the sin reaches the level of major sin (kabira), Allah still retains the name of faith for them. This proves that major sin does not remove iman.
This is the key point against the Mu'tazilite position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أجاب في قوله : "وَإِنَّ طَائِفَتَانِ مِنَ المُؤْمِنِينَ اقْتَتَلُوا ۲۰ أنه كقوله : وَمَنْ يَرْتَدِدْ مِنْكُمْ عَنْ دِينِهِ وقد كان سماه مؤمنا من قبل ، والثانى أن يكون الاقتتال بغير سلاح نحو المجاذبة أو كانوا مجتهدين فلا يخرجون به من الإيمان . فيقال : إذ جرى الأمر بالإصلاح بينهم وتسمية الإخوة بطل معنى الردة ، وقوله : فَقاتِلُوا الَّتي تَبْغِي ، دل أن الباغى كان معلوما ، لا أن كان ثمة ما كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بين أظهرهم أبي لهم الاجتهاد و اجتهاد ، مع أن ذنوبهم إلى ذلك الحد ، ثم دل الأمر بالقتال والصغيرة تكون مغفورة لا يقابل عليها ، على قد كبرت وقد أبقى الله لهم اسم الإيمان ، والله الموفق
Then he answered regarding His statement: 'And if two groups of the believers fight...' (49:9) — that it is like His statement: 'And whoever among you turns back from his religion...' (2:217) and He had called him a believer before. The second point is that the fighting could be without weapons, like grappling, or they were mujtahids (exercising independent judgment), so they do not exit from faith. It is said: Since the matter proceeds to reconciliation between them and the naming of brothers, the meaning of apostasy is invalidated. And His statement: 'Fight the one that transgresses' indicates that the transgressor was known, not that there was any ijtihad when the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, was among them — He refused ijtihad for them, while their sins had reached that extent. Then the command to fight and that a minor sin is forgiven and not punished for, indicates that it had become major (kabira), and yet Allah retained for them the name of faith. And Allah is the Success.
Source pages p. 957

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The opponent cites Quran 49:9, where Allah calls two fighting groups 'believers', to argue that even though they are believers, fighting might remove faith. The author responds by comparing it to the verse on apostasy (2:217), where the person was previously called a believer. He makes two points: first, the fighting might be without weapons (like grappling) or based on ijtihad, which does not remove faith; second, the command to reconcile and the retention of the title 'brothers' invalidates the idea of apostasy. The author further argues that the verse commands fighting the transgressor, which shows that the transgression was known (not an ijtihad error). The fact that Allah retains the name 'believer' for them, despite the major sin of transgression, proves that major sin does not nullify faith.

Key Terms
مؤمن
باغي
اجتهاد
كبيرة
إخوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The belief that fighting between believers removes their faith entirely.
Correction: Imam Maturidi argues that fighting does not necessarily remove faith; the fighters remain brothers and believers in God's sight, even if they commit major sins.

Checkpoint
What does Imam Maturidi argue regarding the verse about fighting believers (49:9)?
A) The fighters are no longer believers.
B) The name 'brothers' indicates they remain believers despite fighting.
C) Only the transgressor loses faith.
D) The verse abrogates the name of faith.

Key Takeaway
Allah retains the name of faith for fighting believers, proving that major sin does not nullify iman.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a Muslim committing a sin, do you still consider them your brother in faith? What would change in your heart if you truly believed that their iman remains intact despite their errors?
?
Think of a Muslim you have distanced yourself from due to their actions. Does this verse compel you to reconcile with them? What step will you take today to restore that brotherhood?
?
Have you ever used your own judgment to label someone's action as a major sin and then concluded they are no longer a believer? How does Imam al-Maturidi's argument challenge that assumption, and what repentance or change of attitude does it demand from you?

Refutation of the Mu'tazilite arguments from brotherhood and retaliation verses
Imam Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazilite use of brotherhood and retaliation verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazilite interpretation of the brotherhood verse (49:10) and the retaliation verse to argue that major sin does not negate religious brotherhood.

Core Idea
Major sin does not remove the believer from the brotherhood of faith.

The Mu'tazilites argued that the Quranic brotherhood of believers implies equality in faith, so a major sinner cannot be called a brother. They also claimed that such a sinner must be cursed. Imam Maturidi responds by showing that the very verse that calls believers brothers also retains the name of faith, and that reform comes through prayer, not curse. Additionally, the retaliation verse uses the term 'brothers' for believers even in the context of murder, proving that brotherhood is religious and persists despite sin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice that the passage contains two separate arguments from the opponent and the author's responses.
The passage is dense with refutations.
2
Identify the two verses cited
The opponent cites two Quranic verses: the brotherhood verse (49:10) and the retaliation verse (al-qisas). Identify how each is used to argue against the view that major sinners remain believers.
3
Understand Maturidi's response to each
For the brotherhood verse, Maturidi points out that Allah retains the name 'believers' at the beginning and 'brothers' at the end. For the retaliation verse, he argues that the term 'brothers' applies in religion despite the sin of killing.
Notice the logical structure of objection and answer.
4
Consider the implication about prayer
Maturidi counters the claim that major sinners must be cursed by asserting that reform comes only through prayer for good and righteousness.
This reinforces the principle of hope for sinners.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في قوله : إِنَّمَا المُؤْمِنُونَ إخوَةٌ ، ٥ بمثل ذلك ، وقد بينا وهمه . ثم على قوله إن صاحب الكبيرة عدو الله لا يسع له الدعاء بالخير ويلزم لعنه ، ومنا الإصلاح إلا الدعاء بالخير والصلاح ، ولا قوة إلا بالله وقال فى آية القصاص وما فيه من تسمية الإخوة : إن الله لم يعد على الإخوة المطلقة ثوابا ولا مدحا ، وإنما كان ذلك فى الإخوة في الدين . فيقال لهم : قد سماهم مؤمنين فى أول الآية ثم أبقى لهم اسم الإخوة في آخرها ، ولا معنى سبق يحتمل حرف ذكر الإخوة إليه ، ثبت أنه في الدين مع إبقاء اسم الإيمان
And he said regarding His statement: 'Indeed the believers are brothers' (49:10) — similarly, and we have explained his error. Then regarding his statement that the committer of a major sin is an enemy of Allah, so it is not permissible to pray for good for him, and cursing him is required, and from us is reform except by praying for good and righteousness — and there is no power except with Allah. And he said regarding the verse of retaliation (al-qisas) and what is in it of naming brothers: 'Allah has not promised the absolute brothers any reward or praise, but that is for brothers in religion.' It is said to them: He called them believers at the beginning of the verse and then retained for them the name of brothers at its end, and there is no prior meaning that the word 'brothers' could be attached to; it is established that it is in religion while retaining the name of faith.
Source pages p. 957

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit covering two related verses. First, the opponent uses Quran 49:10 ('Indeed the believers are brothers') to argue that brotherhood implies equality, so sinners cannot be brothers. The author dismisses this as an error already explained. He then addresses the opponent's claim that a major sinner is an enemy of Allah and must be cursed, not prayed for. The author counters that reform comes only through prayer for good and righteousness. Second, the opponent cites the retaliation verse (probably 2:178-179) which mentions brothers, arguing that the term 'brothers' in that context refers only to religious brothers. The author responds that in the same verse, Allah first calls them believers and then retains the name 'brothers' for them, proving that the brotherhood is religious and that the name of faith is preserved despite the sin of killing.

Key Terms
إخوة
قصاص
كبيرة
دعاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The brotherhood mentioned in the retaliation verse (al-qisas) refers to blood relation or absolute brotherhood, not religious brotherhood.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the same verse calls them believers first and then brothers, proving that the brotherhood is in religion and persists despite major sin.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Maturidi, what does the retaliation verse (ayat al-qisas) prove about the status of a believer who commits a major sin?
A) He is no longer a brother.
B) He retains the name of brother in religion despite sin.
C) The verse only applies to non-sinners.
D) He must be cursed and not prayed for.

Key Takeaway
Imam Maturidi shows that the Quran retains the name of faith and brotherhood for believers despite major sin, refuting the Mu'tazilite position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
